Allah's Existence
beginner
6 min
Blind Imitation of the Tawhid Proof is Insufficient
Sanusi criticizes those who recite the tawhid verse without understanding its logical force.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why merely memorizing or reciting the tawhid verse without grasping its rational proof constitutes blind imitation (taqlid), and how the jurists evaluated such a person's faith.

Core Idea
Reciting a proof without understanding its logic is still blind imitation.

Sanusi moves from the general principle that taqlid is insufficient to a specific example: those who recite the Quranic proof of tawhid (21:22) but do not perceive its rational force. This passage clarifies what counts as true knowledge and why mere memorization, though it might accidentally align with truth, is not praiseworthy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the two shortcomings
Find where Sanusi says the person fails to perceive: (1) the aspect of the impossibility of multiplicity, and (2) the meaning of corruption in the verse. These are the two elements of rational comprehension that are missing.
The verse alone is not enough—understanding the logical implications is required.
3
Understand the jurists' dual ruling
Note that the jurists both rule his deliverance (najat) and his great sin. Why? Because his imitation accidentally coincided with truth, but he resembles those who blindly follow their fathers.
This shows that accidental correctness does not remove blame.
4
Reflect on the condition of certainty
The jurists require that the muqallid have certainty (jazzm) and not abandon his belief if the imitated one does. Consider why this condition is important.
Certainty here is about firm conviction, not rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمَنْ ظَنَّ أنه أحاط بدليل الوحدانية بحفظه أو تلاوته لقوله عَزَّ من قائل : ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتَا ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٢] دون أن يدرك وجهَ استحالة التعدد ، ومعنى الفساد المقصود من الآية . . فهو مقلدٌ، مَثَلُهُ كمثل أي مقلد لاعتقاد آخر، وإنما قرَّر الفقهاء نجاته لكون تقليده وقع اتفاقاً للحقِّ ؛ بشرط جزمه وعدم تركه لمعتقده إن تركه المُقلَّد ، وقالوا بعظيم معصيته لكونه أشبه الذين ألفوا آباءهم ضالين، فهم على آثارهم يهرعون
So whoever thinks that he has encompassed the proof of oneness by memorizing or reciting His saying, Mighty is He: 'If there had been in them gods besides Allah, they would have corrupted' [Al-Anbiya:22] without perceiving the aspect of the impossibility of multiplicity and the meaning of corruption intended by the verse, then he is a blind follower (muqallid), his example is like any follower of another belief. Indeed, the jurists ruled his deliverance because his imitation happened to coincide with the truth, on condition of his certainty and his not abandoning his belief if the imitated one abandons it, and they said his sin is great because he resembles those who found their fathers astray, so they rush in their footsteps.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case of the general principle from the previous lesson: a person who merely memorizes or recites the famous Quranic proof of tawhid—'If there had been in them gods besides Allah, they would have corrupted' (21:22)—without understanding the rational aspect of the impossibility (istihalah) of multiplicity and the exact meaning of 'corruption' (fasad) in the verse, is still a blind follower (muqallid). Such a person's belief is not based on rational comprehension but on imitation. The author notes that jurists (fuqaha') have ruled that such a person is saved (najat) because his imitation coincidentally aligns with the truth, provided he has certainty (jazzm) and does not abandon his creed if the one he imitates abandons it. However, they consider his sin great because he resembles those who blindly follow their fathers, even if they are astray. Thus, mere memorization without rational insight is inadequate.

Key Terms
دليل الوحدانية
التوحيد
المقلد
الاستحالة
الفساد
التقليد
الجزم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The jurists' ruling of 'najat' (salvation) means that blind imitation is acceptable.
Correction: The jurists still call it a great sin because the person resembles those who blindly follow their fathers, even if his imitation coincidentally aligns with truth. True faith requires rational comprehension.

Checkpoint
Why did the jurists consider such a muqallid's sin great?
A) Because he memorized a verse incorrectly
B) Because he resembles those who follow their fathers even if astray
C) Because he did not pray
D) Because he rejected the Quran

Key Takeaway
Reciting a Quranic proof without understanding its rational argument is still blind imitation, and while such a person may be saved by accident, they are guilty of a great sin for resembling those who follow their fathers in error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever recited 'If there were multiple gods, they would have corrupted' without truly grasping why multiplicity is impossible? Are you willing to confront whether your own belief is based on imitation rather than understanding? What step will you take today to move from recitation to comprehension?
?
The jurists say your imitation may save you accidentally, but you still bear great sin for resembling those who blindly follow their fathers in error. Does this description fit you? Are you prepared to examine the rational foundations of your faith, even if it means unsettling the certainty you inherited?
?
When you think about your core Islamic beliefs, how much of what you hold is because you have rationally verified it, and how much is simply what you were taught? If one of your core beliefs were challenged, would you be able to defend it with reasoned arguments, or would you only recite verses? Commit to learning one rational proof for a belief you hold.

Allah's Existence
beginner
3 min
Proof for God's Existence from the World
Sanusi states the proof for God's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the existence of the world is a rational proof for the existence of God.

Core Idea
The world's existence directly proves its Creator.

Sanusi begins with the most fundamental proof: the world itself. Before discussing God's attributes, we must first establish that He exists. This lesson presents that foundational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the concise structure: 'The proof... is the existence of the world.'
2
Understand the implication
The proof is based on the contingency of the world. The world exists and is not self-sufficient, so it requires a cause. This cause is God.
This is a brief premise; further details are in standard kalam.
3
Relate to the lesson
Ask yourself how this proof sets the stage for the subsequent attribute proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجودِهِ تعالى : وجود العالم . ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقِهِ لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسِهِ لاحتاج إلى محلّ أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ . ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ خلقِهِ ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكناتِ أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبَتِ الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائقِ مستحيل .
And the proof for His existence, exalted: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be temporal. And if He were not everlasting, He would not be eternal. And if He were not different from His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsisting, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an attribute. And if He needed a specifier, He would be temporal. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; {And He is the Overpowerer above His servants} (6:18). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient – exalted above that greatly. And if doing or leaving possible things were not permissible in His right, the realities would be inverted, and the inversion of realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides rational proofs for the attributes enumerated earlier. Each proof follows a conditional structure: if the opposite of an attribute were true, a contradiction would follow. The proof for existence starts from the existence of the world, which requires a Creator. Eternity is proven because if not eternal, He would be temporal (hadith), which is impossible for God. Everlastingness follows from eternity. Being different from creation (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) is proven because otherwise He would be like them, implying similarity. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafsih) is proven because need for a locus would make Him an attribute, and need for a specifier would make Him temporal. Oneness is proven by the argument that if there were multiple gods, they would conflict and be overpowered, but God is al-Qahir (the Overpowerer), as cited from the Qur'an. The necessary attributes (qudra, irada, 'ilm, haya) are proven because without them creation would not exist. The attributes of hearing, sight, speech are proven because lacking them would be deficiency. Finally, the permissible attribute (doing or leaving possible acts) is proven because if it were not permissible, the very nature of possibility would be inverted, which is absurd.

Key Terms
وجود العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the proof depends on a specific religious text, but it is purely rational.
Correction: The proof is based on the observed existence of the world and the principle that contingent things need a cause.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proof for God's existence?
A) The Qur'an
B) The existence of the world
C) The attributes of God
D) The angels

Key Takeaway
The existence of the world is a direct rational proof for the existence of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the existence of the world is sufficient proof for God. Look around you right now. Does the world you see actually convince you of His existence, or have you become numb to this proof? What would it take for you to truly see the world as the evidence it is?
?
If someone asked you why you believe in God, would you simply point to the world around you? Or do you rely on other proofs? Are you willing to let the sheer fact of existence be enough for you, or do you still demand more signs?

Proof for God's Eternity and Everlastingness
Sanusi proves God's eternity and everlastingness with conditionals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be eternal and everlasting, as proven by the impossibility of the opposite.

Core Idea
God cannot be temporal; He must be without beginning and end.

Having established God's existence, Sanusi now proves that He must be eternal (without beginning) and everlasting (without end). These two attributes are proven through conditionals that lead to absurdities if denied.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Notice the two parallel conditionals: one for eternity, one for everlastingness.
2
Analyze the first conditional
'If He were not eternal, He would be temporal.' A temporal being is created and needs a creator, but God is the Creator.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the second conditional
'If He were not everlasting, He would not be eternal.' Everlastingness is a consequence of eternity; if He has no end, He must have no beginning.
4
Synthesize
Together, these prove God's timelessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجودِهِ تعالى : وجود العالم . ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقِهِ لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسِهِ لاحتاج إلى محلّ أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ . ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ خلقِهِ ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكناتِ أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبَتِ الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائقِ مستحيل .
And the proof for His existence, exalted: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be temporal. And if He were not everlasting, He would not be eternal. And if He were not different from His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsisting, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an attribute. And if He needed a specifier, He would be temporal. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; {And He is the Overpowerer above His servants} (6:18). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient – exalted above that greatly. And if doing or leaving possible things were not permissible in His right, the realities would be inverted, and the inversion of realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides rational proofs for the attributes enumerated earlier. Each proof follows a conditional structure: if the opposite of an attribute were true, a contradiction would follow. The proof for existence starts from the existence of the world, which requires a Creator. Eternity is proven because if not eternal, He would be temporal (hadith), which is impossible for God. Everlastingness follows from eternity. Being different from creation (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) is proven because otherwise He would be like them, implying similarity. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafsih) is proven because need for a locus would make Him an attribute, and need for a specifier would make Him temporal. Oneness is proven by the argument that if there were multiple gods, they would conflict and be overpowered, but God is al-Qahir (the Overpowerer), as cited from the Qur'an. The necessary attributes (qudra, irada, 'ilm, haya) are proven because without them creation would not exist. The attributes of hearing, sight, speech are proven because lacking them would be deficiency. Finally, the permissible attribute (doing or leaving possible acts) is proven because if it were not permissible, the very nature of possibility would be inverted, which is absurd.

Checkpoint
What would happen if God were not eternal according to the passage?
A) He would be overpowered
B) He would be like His creation
C) He would be temporal
D) He would need a locus

Key Takeaway
God must be eternal and everlasting; otherwise, absurdities follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is truly eternal—without beginning—how does that change the way you view your own life, which has a definite start and end? In what area of your life are you living as if time is irrelevant to your relationship with Him?
?
Knowing that God is everlasting means He will still be there after every single thing you love in this world has perished. What is one attachment you need to loosen today because it distracts you from seeking the One who remains forever?
?
The passage links everlastingness to eternity: if God were not everlasting, He would not be eternal. How does this truth challenge you to think of God not as a 'once upon a time' being but as the ever-present reality that demands a constant response from you right now? What will you do today to make that response real?

Proof for God's Difference from Creation
Sanusi proves God's dissimilarity from creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be different from His creation, as proven by the impossibility of similarity.

Core Idea
God cannot be like His creation; He is absolutely unique.

Sanusi now proves the attribute of mukhalafat lil-hawadith (difference from created things). This is a key principle in Islamic theology: God is unlike anything in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
A single conditional: if not different, then like them.
2
Understand the implication
If God were like His creation, He would be subject to the same limitations and contingency. That would contradict His divinity.
3
Reflect on relevance
This attribute prevents anthropomorphism and ensures God's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجودِهِ تعالى : وجود العالم . ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقِهِ لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسِهِ لاحتاج إلى محلّ أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ . ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ خلقِهِ ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكناتِ أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبَتِ الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائقِ مستحيل .

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson proves that God cannot be like anything you have ever seen or experienced. Is there a part of you that still forms a mental image of God based on your experience with creation? How will you actively replace that with the knowledge that He is utterly different?
?
If God were like creation, He would be imperfect. Do you ever act as if God needs something from you—like your worship or obedience to complete Him? This lesson demands that you correct that thought right now. Write down one way you will remind yourself daily that God is self-sufficient and perfect.
?
The proof is simple but profound: God must be different, or He would be like us. Are there areas in your life where you treat God as if He is distant or limited like a human? This lesson calls you to realign your heart with His absolute uniqueness. What specific step will you take today to honour His incomparability?

Proof for God's Self-Subsistence
Sanusi proves God's self-subsistence via reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God must be self-subsisting (qiyam bi-nafsih), meaning He needs no locus or specifier.

Core Idea
God stands alone; He needs no place or cause.

The attribute of self-subsistence is crucial: God does not depend on anything. Sanusi proves it by showing that needing a locus or specifier would lead to absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note the three conditionals: one for the necessity of self-subsistence and two consequences if denied.
2
Analyze the first part
If not self-subsisting, He would need a locus (mahall) or a specifier (mukhassis).
3
Follow the implications
If He needed a locus, He would be an attribute (which is dependent). If He needed a specifier, He would be temporal (created).
4
Conclude
Both imply dependence, which is impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجودِهِ تعالى : وجود العالم . ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقِهِ لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسِهِ لاحتاج إلى محلّ أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ . ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ خلقِهِ ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكناتِ أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبَتِ الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائقِ مستحيل .
And the proof for His existence, exalted: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be temporal. And if He were not everlasting, He would not be eternal. And if He were not different from His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsisting, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an attribute. And if He needed a specifier, He would be temporal. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; {And He is the Overpowerer above His servants} (6:18). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient – exalted above that greatly. And if doing or leaving possible things were not permissible in His right, the realities would be inverted, and the inversion of realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides rational proofs for the attributes enumerated earlier. Each proof follows a conditional structure: if the opposite of an attribute were true, a contradiction would follow. The proof for existence starts from the existence of the world, which requires a Creator. Eternity is proven because if not eternal, He would be temporal (hadith), which is impossible for God. Everlastingness follows from eternity. Being different from creation (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) is proven because otherwise He would be like them, implying similarity. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafsih) is proven because need for a locus would make Him an attribute, and need for a specifier would make Him temporal. Oneness is proven by the argument that if there were multiple gods, they would conflict and be overpowered, but God is al-Qahir (the Overpowerer), as cited from the Qur'an. The necessary attributes (qudra, irada, 'ilm, haya) are proven because without them creation would not exist. The attributes of hearing, sight, speech are proven because lacking them would be deficiency. Finally, the permissible attribute (doing or leaving possible acts) is proven because if it were not permissible, the very nature of possibility would be inverted, which is absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s self-subsistence means He needs no locus or cause, then your existence depends entirely on Him every moment. Do you live as if your existence is contingent and dependent on God, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What would change if you truly believed you are nothing without Him? This week, try to begin each task by saying 'Bismillah' and acknowledging your dependence.
?
The passage shows that needing a specifier would make something temporal. Your very existence is temporal and caused. How does this reality affect the way you view your life and your purpose? Take a moment to write down one area where you try to be your own 'specifier' (e.g., planning without seeking God's guidance) and commit to praying istikhara for it.
?
God is not an attribute inhering in a substance; He is the Self-Subsistent. Do you sometimes reduce God to a concept or an attribute (e.g., 'The Forgiving') and forget He is the independent Reality that all else depends on? How can you guard against making God into a mental image? This week, memorize the phrase 'Qā'im bi-nafsihi' and repeat it in your sujood to remind yourself of His absolute independence.

Proof for God's Oneness
Sanusi proves God's oneness with a conditional and Quranic support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God is one, based on the impossibility of multiple gods.

Core Idea
If there were more than one god, they would conflict and be overpowered.

Sanusi now proves the oneness of God. The proof is a classic argument: if there were multiple gods, they would inevitably compete, leading to each being overpowered. But God is al-Qahir (the Overpowerer), as confirmed by the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note the conditional and the Quranic proof.
2
Understand the logic
If there were two gods, they would want contrary things. One would overcome the other, so the conquered would not be divine.
3
Connect to the Quran
The verse confirms that God is the Overpowerer, implying oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على وجودِهِ تعالى : وجود العالم . ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقِهِ لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسِهِ لاحتاج إلى محلّ أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ . ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ خلقِهِ ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكناتِ أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبَتِ الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائقِ مستحيل .
And the proof for His existence, exalted: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be temporal. And if He were not everlasting, He would not be eternal. And if He were not different from His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsisting, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an attribute. And if He needed a specifier, He would be temporal. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; {And He is the Overpowerer above His servants} (6:18). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient – exalted above that greatly. And if doing or leaving possible things were not permissible in His right, the realities would be inverted, and the inversion of realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides rational proofs for the attributes enumerated earlier. Each proof follows a conditional structure: if the opposite of an attribute were true, a contradiction would follow. The proof for existence starts from the existence of the world, which requires a Creator. Eternity is proven because if not eternal, He would be temporal (hadith), which is impossible for God. Everlastingness follows from eternity. Being different from creation (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) is proven because otherwise He would be like them, implying similarity. Self-subsistence (qiyam bi-nafsih) is proven because need for a locus would make Him an attribute, and need for a specifier would make Him temporal. Oneness is proven by the argument that if there were multiple gods, they would conflict and be overpowered, but God is al-Qahir (the Overpowerer), as cited from the Qur'an. The necessary attributes (qudra, irada, 'ilm, haya) are proven because without them creation would not exist. The attributes of hearing, sight, speech are proven because lacking them would be deficiency. Finally, the permissible attribute (doing or leaving possible acts) is proven because if it were not permissible, the very nature of possibility would be inverted, which is absurd.

Key Terms
واحد
قهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think oneness is only known from revelation, but here it is rationally proven.
Correction: The rational proof shows that multiple gods would lead to contradiction.

Checkpoint

B) He would be an attribute
C) He would be overpowered
D) He would need a locus

Key Takeaway
God must be one; multiple gods would lead to conflict and each being overpowered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you feel 'overpowered' by trials, do you turn to other 'gods' like distraction or despair? How does knowing that Allah alone is the Overpowerer change how you face that situation? What is one concrete step you can take this week to rely only on Him?
?
The proof says if God were not one, He would be overpowered. Have you ever unconsciously placed anyone or anything in a position of co-rulership over your life—giving them the power to control your happiness or decisions? What will you do to restore His exclusive sovereignty in your heart?

Proof for God's Necessary Attributes: Power, Will, Knowledge, Life
Sanusi proves the necessity of four attributes from creation's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must possess power, will, knowledge, and life, as proven by the existence of creation.

Core Idea
Without these attributes, creation would not exist.

Sanusi now proves that God must have the attributes of power, will, knowledge, and life. These are necessary for Him to be the Creator. The proof is direct: if these attributes were not necessary for God, nothing of His creation would exist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note that four attributes are mentioned together.
2
Understand the implication

3
Reflect on necessity
If any of these were lacking, creation could not come about.

Proof for God's Attributes of Hearing, Sight, and Speech
Sanusi proves the necessity of hearing, sight, speech via perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be described with hearing, sight, and speech, as proven by the necessity of perfection.

Core Idea
Lacking these attributes would imply deficiency, but God is perfect.

After proving the necessary attributes for creation, Sanusi now proves the attributes of hearing, sight, and speech. These are attributes of perfection. If God lacked them, He would be deficient, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
A single conditional: if not described with these, then deficient.
2
Understand perfection
Hearing, sight, and speech are perfections. Their absence in God would be a lack.
3

Sanusi ends with 'exalted above that greatly', affirming God's transcendence.

Proof for the Permissible Attribute: Doing and Leaving Possible Acts
Sanusi proves the permissibility of God's action and inaction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is permissible for God to do or leave possible acts, based on the impossibility of inverting realities.

Core Idea
God is free to act or not; His action is not necessary in itself.

The final attribute Sanusi discusses is the permissible attribute: it is possible for God to do or leave possible acts. This is proven by the absurdity of the opposite: if it were not permissible, realities would be inverted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note the conditional about inversion of realities.
2
Understand the concept
Possible acts are those that are neither necessary nor impossible for God. Their occurrence or non-occurrence is up to Him.
3
Grasp the proof
If it were not permissible (i.e., either necessary or impossible), then what is possible would be otherwise, which would invert the nature of possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Allah's Existence

Proof for God's Existence, Eternity, and Perpetuity
Opening conditional proofs for existence, eternity, and perpetuity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of the world proves God's existence and why God must be eternal and perpetual.

Core Idea
The world's existence points to God, who is necessarily eternal and perpetual.

Sanusi begins his proof for God's attributes by grounding them in the observable world. He argues that the very existence of contingent things requires a necessary cause that is eternal and perpetual. This lesson walks through the first set of conditionals that establish God's timeless existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the conditional 'if...then' structure. Identify the main claim: the world's existence proves God.
2
Analyze the first conditional
'If He were not eternal, He would be originated' – understand the logic: an originated being needs a cause; God cannot be originated.
Think about why 'originated' implies need for a creator.
3
Analyze the second conditional
'If He were not perpetual, He would not be eternal' – note that eternity implies perpetuity. This links the two attributes.
4
Reflect on the proof from the world
The world's existence is the starting point. Ask yourself: how does the existence of changeable things lead to an eternal being?
This is a classic kalam argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة ما سبق من ثبوت الذات والصفات والدليل على وجوده تعالى : وجود العالم ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقه لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسه لاحتاج إلى محل أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً ؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كان شيء من خلقه ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علواً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكنات أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبت الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائق مستحيل .
The proofs for what preceded from the establishment of the essence and attributes: And the proof for His existence, exalted is He: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be originated. And if He were not perpetual, He would not be eternal. And if He were not dissimilar to His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsistent, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an accident. And if He needed a specifier, He would be originated. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; (He is the Omnipotent over His servants). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient—exalted is He above that, a great exaltation. And if the doing or leaving of contingent things were not permissible for Him, the realities would be inverted, and inverting realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a series of conditional (reductio ad absurdum) proofs for the necessary attributes of God. It begins by stating that the proof for God's existence is the existence of the world (a standard kalam argument). Then it proceeds attribute by attribute: if God were not eternal (qadīm), He would be originated (ḥādith); if not perpetual (bāqin), He would not be eternal; if not dissimilar to creation, He would be like them; if not self-subsistent, He would need a locus (maḥall) or specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ); if He needed a locus, He would be an accident (ṣifa); if He needed a specifier, He would be originated; if He were not one (wāḥid), He would be overpowered (maqhūr)—citing the Quranic verse 'He is the Omnipotent over His servants.' Then the necessary attributes of power (qudra), will (irāda), knowledge (‘ilm), and life (ḥayāt) are proven: without them, no creation would exist. Then hearing (sam‘), sight (baṣar), and speech (kalām) are shown necessary to avoid deficiency (naqṣ). Finally, the permissibility (jawāz) of God's actions—doing or leaving contingent acts—is established; otherwise, the very nature of realities would be inverted, which is impossible. The argument follows the method of 'if not A, then B, and B is false, so A is necessary.'

Key Terms

صفات

God's existence is proven by the world's existence, and He must be both eternal and perpetual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If God is perpetual—always remaining—then what are you clinging to that will not remain? Be honest: what temporary thing are you afraid to let go of, and what would it mean to entrust it to the One who never passes away?

Proof for God's Dissimilarity and Self-Subsistence
Conditional proofs for God's dissimilarity to creation and self-subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be unlike His creation and self-subsistent, and the consequences of denying these attributes.

Core Idea
God cannot be like His creation nor dependent on anything; He is absolutely unique and self-sufficient.

Sanusi continues his series of conditionals to prove that God is dissimilar to His creation and self-subsistent. If He were like them, He would be contingent; if He needed a locus or specifier, He would be an accident or originated. These proofs reinforce God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that it contains two main conditionals: one for dissimilarity and one for self-subsistence, with sub-conditionals.
2
Understand the dissimilarity conditional
'If He were not dissimilar, He would be like them' – being like creation implies limitation and contingency, which cannot apply to God.
This guards against anthropomorphism.
3
Analyze the self-subsistence conditional
'If He were not self-subsistent, He would need a locus or specifier' – needing a locus makes Him an accident; needing a specifier makes Him originated.
Accidents are temporary; specifiers are causes for existence.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
These conditionals together establish that God is independent and unlike anything else. Reflect on why this is foundational for tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة ما سبق من ثبوت الذات والصفات والدليل على وجوده تعالى : وجود العالم ولو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن باقياً لم يكن قديماً ، ولو لم يكن مخالفاً لخلقه لكان مثلهم ، ولو لم يكن قائماً بنفسه لاحتاج إلى محل أو مخصص ، ولو افتقر إلى محل لكان صفةً ، ولو احتاج إلى مخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولو لم يكن واحداً لكان مقهوراً ؛ ﴿ وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ﴾ ولو لم تجب له القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة لما كان شيء من خلقه ، ولو لم يتصف بالسمع والبصر والكلام لكان ناقصاً ، تعالى عن ذلك علواً كبيراً . ولو لم يكن فعل الممكنات أو تركها جائزاً في حقه تعالى لانقلبت الحقائق ، وقلب الحقائق مستحيل .
The proofs for what preceded from the establishment of the essence and attributes: And the proof for His existence, exalted is He: the existence of the world. And if He were not eternal, He would be originated. And if He were not perpetual, He would not be eternal. And if He were not dissimilar to His creation, He would be like them. And if He were not self-subsistent, He would need a locus or a specifier. And if He needed a locus, He would be an accident. And if He needed a specifier, He would be originated. And if He were not one, He would be overpowered; (He is the Omnipotent over His servants). And if power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist. And if He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient—exalted is He above that, a great exaltation. And if the doing or leaving of contingent things were not permissible for Him, the realities would be inverted, and inverting realities is impossible.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a series of conditional (reductio ad absurdum) proofs for the necessary attributes of God. It begins by stating that the proof for God's existence is the existence of the world (a standard kalam argument). Then it proceeds attribute by attribute: if God were not eternal (qadīm), He would be originated (ḥādith); if not perpetual (bāqin), He would not be eternal; if not dissimilar to creation, He would be like them; if not self-subsistent, He would need a locus (maḥall) or specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ); if He needed a locus, He would be an accident (ṣifa); if He needed a specifier, He would be originated; if He were not one (wāḥid), He would be overpowered (maqhūr)—citing the Quranic verse 'He is the Omnipotent over His servants.' Then the necessary attributes of power (qudra), will (irāda), knowledge (‘ilm), and life (ḥayāt) are proven: without them, no creation would exist. Then hearing (sam‘), sight (baṣar), and speech (kalām) are shown necessary to avoid deficiency (naqṣ). Finally, the permissibility (jawāz) of God's actions—doing or leaving contingent acts—is established; otherwise, the very nature of realities would be inverted, which is impossible. The argument follows the method of 'if not A, then B, and B is false, so A is necessary.'

Proof for God's Oneness
Conditional proof for God's oneness with Quranic support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be one and the logical consequence of denying His oneness.

Core Idea
If God were not one, He would be overpowered – but He is the Omnipotent, so He is necessarily one.

Sanusi now argues for God's oneness (tawhid). Using a conditional proof, he shows that if God were not one, He would be subject to being overpowered, which contradicts His absolute sovereignty. A Quranic verse reinforces the conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the conditional structure and the Quranic citation.
2
Understand the conditional
'If He were not one, He would be overpowered' – more than one god would lead to conflict and subjugation, as per the Quranic argument.
This is a classic argument against polytheism.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verse
The verse 'He is the Omnipotent over His servants' confirms that God is all-powerful and cannot be overpowered, thus must be one.
4
Connect to tawhid
This proof establishes that God's oneness is necessary for His absolute sovereignty. Think about why multiple gods would entail weakness.

Proof for God's Essential Attributes: Power, Will, Knowledge, and Life
Conditional proof for the necessity of power, will, knowledge, and life in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must possess power, will, knowledge, and life as necessary attributes for creation to exist.

Core Idea
Without power, will, knowledge, and life, nothing in creation would exist – so God must possess them.

Sanusi presents a conditional argument that ties God's creative action to His attributes. If these four attributes were not necessary for God, then nothing would have been created. This establishes them as essential to His nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that it is a single conditional with a compound subject: power, will, knowledge, and life.
2
Understand the conditional logic
'If power, will, knowledge, and life were not necessary for Him, nothing of His creation would exist.' This means creation depends on these attributes.
3
Reflect on each attribute
Power enables action, will chooses, knowledge designs, life is the basis. Consider why each is needed for a creator.
4
Connect to the overall argument
This proof shows that God's attributes are not arbitrary but necessary for His role as creator. They are inseparable from His essence.

Proof for God's Attributes of Perfection and Permissibility of Actions
Conditional proofs for auditory, visual, speech attributes and the permissibility of divine actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be described with hearing, sight, and speech, and why His actions must be permissible (not constrained).

Core Idea
Without hearing, sight, and speech, God would be deficient; without permissibility, realities would be inverted.

Sanusi concludes his series of proofs by affirming that God must have attributes of perfection – hearing, sight, and speech – and that His actions must be free and permissible. Denying these would lead to absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two conditionals: one for the attributes of perfection, one for permissibility.
2
Understand the first conditional
'If He were not described with hearing, sight, and speech, He would be deficient' – lack of these attributes implies imperfection, impossible for God.
These are sometimes called 'sifāt ma‘nawiyya' or attributes of perfection.
3
Understand the second conditional
'If doing or leaving contingent things were not permissible for Him, realities would be inverted' – God's actions must be free; otherwise, the nature of possibility would change.
Contingent things are those that can exist or not; God's choice is not forced.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
These last conditionals complete the portrait of God as perfect and free. Realities would be 'inverted' if God were compelled.

Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
The Necessity of Allah's Existence
Sanusi proves divine existence from contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why existence is a necessary attribute of Allah and how the dependence of contingent beings proves it.

Core Idea
All contingent things depend on a necessary being for their existence.

Sanusi begins his enumeration of Allah's necessary attributes with existence (al-wujūd). He argues that contingent things are in need of a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ), and their very existence points to a necessary cause. In this lesson, we explore this foundational proof that underlies all subsequent attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud, noting the concise logical structure. Pay attention to the phrase 'لتوقف وجود الحوادث على وجوده' which is the core argument.
The passage begins with the author's directive 'فاعلم'—he is teaching you specifically.
2
Identify the proof structure
The argument has two parts: (1) The existence of contingent beings (ḥawādith) depends on Allah's existence. (2) The proof of their contingency is that they require a specifier. Observe how the second part supports the first.
'لزومها لما يفتقر إلى المخصص'—contingents are inherently in need of something to specify their existence out of possibilities.
3
Reflect on the deeper implication
Ask yourself: If contingent beings did not need a specifier, would the proof for divine existence still hold? This understanding is crucial for grasping the entire kalam framework.
This connects to the broader kalām argument from contingency, a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفات الواجبة له سبحانه ] فإذا عرفت هذا فاعلم : أنَّه يجبُ لمولانا جل وعزَّ الوجود ؛ لتوقف وجودِ الحوادثِ على وجودِهِ تعالى ودليل حدوثها : لزومها لما يفتقر إلى المخصص ويجبُ لهُ تعالى القدمُ والبقاء ، وإلا كان محتاجاً إلى الفاعل ، فيكون حادثاً ، فيجبُ لهُ من الحدوث ما وجبَ لسائرِ الحوادثِ ، بل يكون حينئذ وجوده مستحيلاً ؛ لما يلزم على تقدير حدوثِهِ مِنَ الدور أو التسلسل المستحيلينِ ويجب أن يكون تعالى مخالفاً في ذاتِهِ وصفاته لكلّ ما سواهُ مِنَ الحوادث ، وإلا كان حادثاً مثلها ويجب لهُ تعالى أنْ يكونَ قائماً بنفسِهِ ؛ أي : ذاتاً موصوفاً بالصفاتِ ، غنياً عن المحل والفاعل ؛ إذْ لو كانَ في محل لكانَ صفةً ، فيلزم ألا يتّصف بالصفاتِ الوجودية ولا لوازمها ؛ إذ لو قبلَتِ الصفة صفة وجودية .. لزم ألا
[The Attributes Necessary for Him, Exalted is He] Now that you have understood this, know: It is necessary for our Lord, Glorious and Exalted, to have existence (al-wujūd), because the existence of contingent things depends on His existence. The proof of their contingency is their being subject to what is in need of a specifier. And it is necessary for Him, Exalted, to have pre-eternity (al-qidam) and everlastingness (al-baqā'), because otherwise He would be in need of an agent, and thus would be contingent; then the state of contingency would be necessary for Him just as it is necessary for the rest of contingents—nay, at that time His existence would be impossible, because what would follow from the assumption of His contingency is circularity or an infinite regress, both of which are impossible. And it is necessary that He, Exalted, be different (mukhālif) in His essence and attributes from everything other than Him among contingent things, because otherwise He would be contingent like them. And it is necessary for Him, Exalted, to be self-subsistent (qā'imun bi-nafsihi), meaning: an essence qualified by attributes, independent of a substrate and an agent; for if He were in a substrate, He would be an accident, and then it would follow that He is not qualified by existential attributes nor their concomitants; because if an accident were to accept an existential attribute... it would follow that...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a proof passage for several necessary divine attributes. It begins by asserting that existence (al-wujūd) is necessary for Allah, evidenced by the dependence of contingent beings (ḥawādith) on Him; their contingency is proven by their need for a specifier (mukhaṣṣiṣ). Then it asserts pre-eternity (al-qidam) and everlastingness (al-baqā'): if He were not eternal, He would need an agent, making Him contingent (ḥādith), which would entail the same contingency as other contingent beings—and worse, His existence would become impossible because assuming His contingency leads to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both impossible. Next, it asserts that He must be different (mukhālif) from all contingent things in essence and attributes, otherwise He would be like them and thus contingent. Finally, it asserts that He must be self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi), i.e., an essence with attributes, independent of a substrate and agent; if He were in a substrate, He would be an accident, which cannot be described with existential attributes—all this shows His independence and uniqueness. The passage ends abruptly mid-argument regarding accidents accepting attributes.

Key Terms
وجود
حوادث
مخصص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that existence is not necessarily an attribute of Allah because existence is common to all things.
Correction: The passage argues that Allah's existence is necessary (wājib) while the existence of contingent things is merely possible (jāʾiz). The proof shows that contingent existence points to a necessary source, so Allah's existence is qualitatively different.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proof that contingent things are contingent?
A) They are subject to change.
B) They are in need of a specifier.
C) They are finite.
D) They were created in time.

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is necessary because all contingent beings depend on a specifier, which ultimately points to a necessary being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own existence is contingent and depends on Allah's specification every single moment, how does that change the way you view your independence? Can you genuinely thank Allah for sustaining you right now, not just in the past?
?
What worldly things do you treat as 'necessary' in your heart—like your health, relationships, or wealth? How does knowing that only Allah is truly necessary loosen your attachment to them?
?
When you wake up tomorrow, what is one concrete action you can take to remind yourself that you are a 'contingent being' needing Allah's specification—not just a habit, but a real heart check?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
Pre-Eternity and Everlastingness of Allah
Sanusi proves pre-eternity and everlastingness via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why pre-eternity (qidam) and everlastingness (baqā') are necessary attributes of Allah, and the logical consequences of denying them.

Core Idea
If Allah were not eternal, He would be contingent like other beings, leading to impossibility.

Having established that existence is necessary for Allah, Sanusi now proves that this existence must be eternal—without beginning (qidam) and without end (baqā'). He demonstrates that if Allah were not eternal, He would need a creator, making Him contingent, and that would lead to absurd consequences like circularity or infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for pre-eternity and everlastingness
Read the Arabic text that argues: if Allah were not eternal, He would need an agent (fāʿil) and thus be contingent (ḥādith). Then the same contingency would apply to Him as to other things.
Pay attention to the phrase 'وإلا كان محتاجاً إلى الفاعل'—this is the key conditional.
2
Understand the stronger consequence
The passage then says: not only would He be contingent, but His existence would be impossible because assuming His contingency leads to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul). Understand why these are impossible in kalām.
Circularity means A depends on B and B depends on A; regress is an infinite chain without a first cause.
3
Connect to the overall proof
The necessity of pre-eternity and everlastingness directly follows from the proof of existence. If Allah's existence is necessary, it cannot have a beginning or end, because then it would be contingent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Allah's Difference from Creation and Self-Subsistence
Sanusi proves Allah's dissimilarity to creation and His self-subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah must be absolutely different from all contingent things (mukhālafa) and why He is self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi), independent of any substrate or agent.

Core Idea
Allah's essence and attributes are unlike any created thing, and He exists independently.

After establishing existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness, Sanusi adds two more necessary attributes: being different from all contingent things (mukhālafa li-l-ḥawādith) and being self-subsistent (qiyām bi-nafs). These attributes emphasize Allah's transcendence and independence. In this lesson, we see how any similarity to creation would imply contingency, and how being in a substrate would reduce Him to an accident.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on being different
Read the Arabic: it says Allah must be different (mukhālif) in His essence and attributes from everything else, otherwise He would be contingent like them.
The phrase 'وإلا كان حادثاً مثلها' shows the consequence of similarity.
2
Read the passage on self-subsistence
Read the definition: qā'im bi-nafsihi means a self-subsistent essence described with attributes, independent of a substrate (maḥall) and an agent. The passage gives a proof: if He were in a substrate, He would be an accident, and accidents cannot accept existential attributes, making it impossible for Him to be described with attributes.
The argument ends abruptly but the gist is that Allah cannot be an accident.
3
Synthesize both attributes
Both attributes reinforce Allah's uniqueness. Being different ensures He is not part of the contingent world; being self-subsistent ensures He is not dependent on anything else. Together, they complete the picture of a transcendent, independent Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The World as a Sign: Understanding 'Al-'Aalam'
Sanusi explains the derivation of 'al-'aalam' from 'sign' or 'knowledge'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the world is called 'al-'aalam' and how it serves as a sign leading to knowledge of Allah.

Core Idea
The world is a sign; its very name points to its Creator.

Before Sanusi presents his main proof from 'Rabb al-'Aalameen', he establishes the conceptual foundation: the word 'al-'aalam' (the world) itself indicates a sign or knowledge of the Creator. This lesson explores that linguistic and theological insight.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening verses and context
Read the passage where Sanusi discusses the polytheists' challenge and the call to reflect on creation. Notice how he uses Quranic verses to emphasize that every event leads to knowledge of Allah.
The verses from Surah ar-Ra'd, Al Imran, and al-A'raf are cited.
2
Identify the two derivations of 'al-'aalam'
Look for the sentence that explains the two possible derivations: from 'al-'alaamah' (sign) or from 'al-'ilm' (knowledge). Understand why each is fitting.
This shows the world's purpose as a pointer to its Creator.
3
Reflect on how this sets up the proof
Consider how this linguistic foundation prepares the reader for the proof from 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شركاء مِنَ الحوادثِ ؛ فقال تعالى : ﴿وَجَعَلُوا لِلَّهِ شُرَكَاءَ قُلْ سَمُوهُمْ ﴾ الرعد : (٣٣) أي : اذكروا أوصافَهُم حتى يُنظَرَ : أفيها ما يَصلُحُ للألوهية أم لا . ويحتمل أن تكونَ المناسبة : أنَّ كلَّ حادث يحصلُ العلم للناظرِ فيهِ بما يجب للمولى العظيمِ مِنْ عَلِيٍّ الصفاتِ ، ويُنزّههُ عن سماتِ المحدثاتِ ، ولهذا قالَ  َجلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لَاَيَتِ لِأُولِي الْأَلْبَبِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٩٠] ، وقال جل وعلا : ﴿ أَوَلَمْ يَنظُرُوا فِي مَلَكُوتِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا خَلَقَ اللَّهُ مِن شَيْءٍ [الأعراف : ١٨٥] ، والآيات في ذلك كثيرة . ، فالمناسبة الأولى في وضع اللغة والاصطلاحِ : تقتضي أنَّ العالَمَ مأخوذ من العلامة والمناسبة الثانية : تقتضي أنَّهُ مَأخوذُ مِنَ العِلْمِ . وذِكْرُ هذا الوصف ؛ وهو ( ربُّ العالمينَ ) بعد ( الحمدُ للهِ ) شبه البرهان بعد الدعوى ؛ لأنَّهُ لمَّا ادَّعى في الجملة الأولى أنَّ كلَّ كمال فهو الله تعالى وحدَهُ ، لا يُمدَحُ عليه في الحقيقة سواه ، وقد عرفتَ أنَّ الكمالَ إمَّا قديمٌ وإِمَّا حادث .. أتى بما يدلُّ على أنَّ كلا الكمالين لهُ تعالى ؛ بمعنى : أنَّ الأول وصفه ، والثاني فعله ، والدليل على ذلكَ : العوالم ؛ لأنَّه قد قام البرهان القطعي على حدوثها من جهة تغيُّرها الذي آذنَتْ بهِ التربية المأخوذةُ مِنْ لفظ ( رَبِّ ) ، ومِنْ جهة احتياجها إلى المُخصِّص في اختصاصها ببعض ما تقبلُهُ مِنْ مقدار وصفة وغيرهما ، وقد أشعر أيضاً بالاحتياج إلى المخصص : الإتيان بالجمع في ( العالمينَ ) ؛ فإنَّهُ مُؤذِنٌ بالاختلاف في المقادير والصفاتِ والأزمنة والأمكنة ، معَ قبولِ كلِّ مقدار غيره وصفته وزمانه ومكانه ، فلو وقع ذلكَ مِنْ غيرِ فاعل .. لزمَ الجمع بين متنافيين ؛ وهما مساواة أحد الأمرين لصاحبه ورجحانه عليه بلا سبب، وذلك معلوم الاستحالة . فإذاً ؛ هذا الوصف ؛ وهو ( ربُّ العالمينَ ) مُؤذِنٌ بحدوثِ جميعِ العوالم مِنْ جهةِ المضافِ(۱) ؛ لإشعارِهِ بعموم التربية للعوالمِ المستلزمة للتغير في جميعها ، وهو دليل على الحدوثِ والافتقار للمحدثِ ، ومِنْ جهة المضاف إليه ؛ لإشعارِهِ بسبب جمعيَّتِهِ وعمومه باختلافِ أصنافِ العوالم وأنواعها وأجناسها في مقاديرها وصفاتها وأزمنتها وأمكنتها وجهاتها ، معَ قَبولِ مادَّةِ كلَّ واحدٍ منها لِمَا حصلَ لغيره ، وذلكَ يستلزم (۲) حدوثها وافتقارها إلى المخصص ولمَّا كانَ الإحداث والإيجاد موقوفين على كمال ألوهية الموجدِ ، واتصافه (۳) : بوجوبِ الوجودِ ، والقدم ، والبقاء ، والقيام بالنفس والمخالفة للحوادثِ ، والوحدانية ، والحياة ، وعموم القدرة والإرادة لجميع الممكنات ، وعموم العلم لجميع الواجبات والجائزات
partners from the events; so He said, the Most High: {And they have attributed to Allah partners. Say: 'Name them'} ar-Ra'd 13:33, i.e., mention their descriptions so that it may be seen: is there among them what is suitable for divinity or not. And it is possible that the suitability is: that every event brings knowledge to the one who reflects on it of what is necessary for the great Master of lofty attributes, and declares Him free from the marks of originated things, and for this He said, exalted be He: {Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs for those of understanding} Al Imran 3:190, and He said, exalted and majestic: {Did they not look into the dominion of the heavens and the earth and everything that Allah has created} al-A'raf 7:185, and the verses in that regard are many. So the first suitability in the setting of language and terminology requires that the world (al-'aalam) is derived from the sign (al-'alaamah), and the second suitability requires that it is derived from knowledge (al-'ilm). And the mention of this description, which is 'Lord of the worlds' (Rabb al-'Aalameen) after 'Praise be to Allah' is like a proof after a claim; because when He claimed in the first sentence that every perfection belongs to Allah alone, no one else is truly praised for it, and you have known that perfection is either eternal or contingent, He brought what indicates that both perfections belong to Him, the Most High; meaning: the first is His attribute, and the second is His action. And the evidence for that is the worlds; because the definitive proof has been established of their contingency from the aspect of their change which the education (al-tarbiyah) taken from the word 'Lord' (Rabb) indicated, and from the aspect of their need for a specific cause (al-mukhaṣṣiṣ) in their being specified with some of what they accept of quantity, quality, and other than them. And it has also indicated the need for a specific cause: the use of the plural in 'the worlds'; for it indicates difference in quantities, qualities, times, places, while each quantity accepts other than its quantity, quality, time, and place. So if that occurred without a doer... then it would necessitate the combination of two mutually exclusive things: equality of one of the two things with its counterpart and its preference over it without a cause, and that is known to be impossible. So then this description, which is 'Lord of the worlds', indicates the contingency of all the worlds from the aspect of the first part of the construct (al-muḍāf); because it indicates the generality of education for all worlds, which entails change in all of them, and it is a proof of contingency and need for the originator; and from the aspect of the second part of the construct (al-muḍāf ilayh); because it indicates, by its being a plural and its generality, the difference of the kinds of worlds and their types and genera in their quantities, qualities, times, places, and directions, while the matter of each one of them accepts what has occurred for another, and that necessitates their contingency and their need for the specific cause. And when creation and bringing into existence are dependent on the perfection of the divinity of the Creator, and His being qualified with: necessary existence, eternity, everlastingness, self-subsistence, being different from contingent things, oneness, life, generality of power and will over all possible things, and generality of knowledge over all necessary and contingent things.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the world's contingency derived from the Quranic phrase 'Rabb al-'Alamin' (Lord of the worlds) in Surah al-Fatihah. The author begins by addressing the broader context of shirk (associating partners with Allah). He cites the verse 'And they have attributed to Allah partners. Say: Name them' (13:33) to challenge the polytheists to describe their alleged partners to see if they possess divine attributes. He then suggests that every event (حادث) when reflected upon leads to knowledge of Allah's attributes and transcendence. This is supported by verses calling for reflection on the creation of the heavens and earth.

Next, the author discusses the derivation of the word 'al-'aalam' (the world). In language and terminology, it is either derived from 'al-'alaamah' (sign) because it is a sign of its Creator, or from 'al-'ilm' (knowledge) because it leads to knowledge of its Creator.

Then comes the main argument: the placement of 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' after 'al-Hamdu lillah' is like a proof after a claim. The claim is that all perfection belongs to Allah alone. Perfection is either eternal (an attribute of Allah) or contingent (His actions). The evidence for this claim is the worlds (al-'awaalim).

The proof proceeds in two ways:
1. From the word 'Rabb' (Lord): 'Rabb' implies tarbiyah (education, nurturing, causing to grow), which involves change. Change indicates contingency (huduth). Therefore, the worlds, being subject to God's nurturing, are contingent.
2. From the plural 'al-'Aalameen' (the worlds): The plural indicates diversity among the worlds in quantities, qualities, times, and places. Each thing could have been different from what it is. If this diversity occurred without a specific cause (mukhaṣṣiṣ), it would require either equality (all things being the same) or preference without a reason—both impossible. Therefore, a specific cause is needed to choose one state over another, proving the contingency of the worlds.

Thus, the phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' indicates the contingency of all worlds from both its parts: the first part (al-muḍāf) emphasizes universal education implying change, and the second part (al-muḍāf ilayh) emphasizes diversity requiring a specific cause.

Finally, the author notes that creation depends on the perfection of the Creator's divinity, listing necessary attributes such as necessary existence, eternity, life, power, will, and knowledge. This connects the contingency argument to the attributes of the Creator. The passage ends mid-sentence as it enumerates these attributes, leaving the conclusion implicit.

Key Terms
العالم (al-'aalam)
العلامة (al-'alaamah)
العلم (al-'ilm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, from which two words is 'al-'aalam' (the world) possibly derived?
A) 'al-'alaamah' (sign) and 'al-'ilm' (knowledge)
B) 'al-urd' (earth) and 'al-sama' (sky)
C) 'al-khalq' (creation) and 'al-amr' (command)
D) 'al-zaman' (time) and 'al-makan' (place)

Key Takeaway
The world's very name indicates that it is a sign leading to knowledge of its Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the world around you—the sky, the earth, your own existence—do you automatically see it as a sign pointing to its Creator, or do you treat it as merely a backdrop to your daily concerns? What would it take for that shift in vision to become your constant habit?
?
Sanusi says the world is derived from 'knowledge' because it leads to knowledge of Allah. How much of your knowledge about Allah comes from actively reflecting on the events of your life versus from hearsay or books? Are you willing to commit to spending time each day in silent reflection on one creation—a tree, a cloud, a blessing—until it yields fresh knowledge of Him?
?
The polytheists named their partners but could not describe attributes worthy of divinity. Which 'partners'—people, possessions, ambitions—do you habitually give a status in your heart that rivals the Creator's? Will you today name them and then examine them against the standard of this lesson: are they signs pointing to Allah, or distractions claiming His place?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
The Proof from 'Rabb al-'Aalameen': Contingency of the Worlds
Sanusi derives contingency from 'Rabb' and the plural 'al-'Aalameen'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' provides a proof for the contingency of the worlds from both its parts.

Core Idea
'Rabb' implies change; 'al-'Aalameen' implies diversity; both point to contingency.

Having established that the world is a sign, Sanusi now uses the very words of the Fatihah to construct a logical proof. The phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' is not merely praise; it contains a demonstration that the worlds are contingent and need a Creator. This lesson unpacks the two arguments embedded in the phrase.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure: proof after claim
Notice that Sanusi presents the phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' after 'al-Hamdu lillah' as a proof supporting the claim that all perfection belongs to Allah. The claim is that perfection is either eternal (Allah's attribute) or contingent (His action), and the worlds provide evidence.
2
Examine the proof from 'Rabb'
The word 'Rabb' implies tarbiyah (education/nurturing), which entails change. Change is a sign of contingency (huduth). Therefore, the worlds, being subject to God's nurturing, are contingent.
This is the first argument: from the first part of the construct (al-muḍāf).
3
Examine the proof from the plural 'al-'Aalameen'
The plural form indicates diversity among the worlds in quantities, qualities, times, and places. Each thing could have been different. If this diversity occurred without a specific cause (mukhaṣṣiṣ), it would require either equality or preference without reason—both impossible. Therefore, a specific cause is needed, proving contingency.
This is the second argument: from the second part (al-muḍāf ilayh).
4
Connect to the necessity of the Creator's attributes
Sanusi concludes that creation depends on the perfection of the Creator's divinity, listing necessary attributes such as necessary existence, eternity, life, power, will, and knowledge.
This links the contingency argument to the attributes of Allah.

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the world's contingency derived from the Quranic phrase 'Rabb al-'Alamin' (Lord of the worlds) in Surah al-Fatihah. The author begins by addressing the broader context of shirk (associating partners with Allah). He cites the verse 'And they have attributed to Allah partners. Say: Name them' (13:33) to challenge the polytheists to describe their alleged partners to see if they possess divine attributes. He then suggests that every event (حادث) when reflected upon leads to knowledge of Allah's attributes and transcendence. This is supported by verses calling for reflection on the creation of the heavens and earth.

Next, the author discusses the derivation of the word 'al-'aalam' (the world). In language and terminology, it is either derived from 'al-'alaamah' (sign) because it is a sign of its Creator, or from 'al-'ilm' (knowledge) because it leads to knowledge of its Creator.

Then comes the main argument: the placement of 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' after 'al-Hamdu lillah' is like a proof after a claim. The claim is that all perfection belongs to Allah alone. Perfection is either eternal (an attribute of Allah) or contingent (His actions). The evidence for this claim is the worlds (al-'awaalim).

The proof proceeds in two ways:
1. From the word 'Rabb' (Lord): 'Rabb' implies tarbiyah (education, nurturing, causing to grow), which involves change. Change indicates contingency (huduth). Therefore, the worlds, being subject to God's nurturing, are contingent.
2. From the plural 'al-'Aalameen' (the worlds): The plural indicates diversity among the worlds in quantities, qualities, times, and places. Each thing could have been different from what it is. If this diversity occurred without a specific cause (mukhaṣṣiṣ), it would require either equality (all things being the same) or preference without a reason—both impossible. Therefore, a specific cause is needed to choose one state over another, proving the contingency of the worlds.

Thus, the phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' indicates the contingency of all worlds from both its parts: the first part (al-muḍāf) emphasizes universal education implying change, and the second part (al-muḍāf ilayh) emphasizes diversity requiring a specific cause.

Finally, the author notes that creation depends on the perfection of the Creator's divinity, listing necessary attributes such as necessary existence, eternity, life, power, will, and knowledge. This connects the contingency argument to the attributes of the Creator. The passage ends mid-sentence as it enumerates these attributes, leaving the conclusion implicit.

Key Terms

التربية (al-tarbiyah)
الحدوث (al-huduth)
المخصص (al-mukhaṣṣiṣ)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'رب العالمين' is merely an honorary title without theological weight.
Correction: Sanusi shows it is a proof of the world's contingency, containing two arguments that demonstrate the need for a Creator.

Checkpoint
Why does the word 'رب' (Lord) indicate the contingency of the world according to Sanusi?
A) Because it implies ownership, and ownership requires a possessed thing which is temporal.
B) Because it implies education (تربية) which entails change, and change is a sign of contingency.
C) Because it is a name of Allah and all names of Allah are proofs of existence.
D) Because it is a verbal noun and all verbal nouns indicate temporality.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' itself proves the contingency of all worlds and the necessity of a specific Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The diversity in creation demands a specific cause. Look at the differences between you and others—your abilities, health, opportunities. Do you truly see these as products of deliberate divine selection, or do you sometimes treat them as random? How would your gratitude and complaints change if you internalized that every detail has a specific Cause? Commit to one specific difference you will consciously attribute to Allah's choice today.
?
Sanusi says the phrase 'Rabb al-'Aalameen' is a proof after a claim. What claim are you making about your life that lacks this kind of evidence? Perhaps you claim that your success is your own doing, or that your difficulties are meaningless. Where do you need to align your belief with the fact that everything is contingent and dependent on Allah? Write down one area and a concrete action to acknowledge His control.
?
If you truly believe that everything in your life—every change, every diversity—is a sign of contingency pointing to a specific Creator, why do you still worry about outcomes as if they are random? Choose one fear you have about the future. How does the certainty that Allah is the specific Cause of all things dismantle that fear? What can you do today to live out that trust?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
The Contingency of the Worlds from 'Rabb al-'ālamīn'
Sanusi uses the plural 'al-'ālamīn' to prove contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the plural form 'al-'ālamīn' in the Qur'anic phrase 'Rabb al-'ālamīn' provides a rational argument for the contingency of all worlds and the need for a specific agent (mukhaṣṣiṣ).

Core Idea
Diversity without a cause is impossible; thus the worlds must be contingent.

Sanusi begins by drawing attention to the grammatical structure of 'Rabb al-'ālamīn' (Lord of the worlds). The plural 'al-'ālamīn' indicates that the worlds differ in measures, attributes, times, and places, yet each could have been otherwise. If such diversity occurred without a cause, it would involve a logical contradiction – the combination of two mutually exclusive states. Therefore, a specific agent (mukhaṣṣiṣ) must exist, implying the contingency of all worlds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'وصفة وغيرهما' to 'وذلك يستلزم حدوثها وافتقارها إلى المخصص' and its translation. Notice how Sanusi uses the plural form as a starting point.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two aspects of the argument
The passage presents two angles: from the added (al-mudāf) – 'Rabb' implying upbringing and change – and from the added-to (al-mudāf ilayh) – 'al-'ālamīn' implying diversity. Note how each leads to contingency.
These two aspects are complementary.
3
Understand the logical impossibility
Focus on the reasoning: without a cause, two equal things would be unequal, which is impossible. This is the key to demanding a specific agent.
This is a standard kalam argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the description 'Rabb al-'ālamīn' indicates the contingency of all worlds and their need for an originator. Ask yourself: why is this significant for theology?
